<p><b>Gheorghe "Gică" Hagi</b> (<small>Romanian pronunciation:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Romanian" title="Help:IPA/Romanian">[ˈɡe̯orɡe ˈhad͡ʒi]</a></span><small class="nowrap">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Ro-Gheorghe_Hagi.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c4/Ro-Gheorghe_Hagi.ogg" class="internal" title="Ro-Gheorghe Hagi.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>; born 5 February 1965) is a Romanian former professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">footballer</a>, considered one of the best <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Attacking_midfielder" title="Midfielder">attacking midfielders</a> in Europe during the 1980s and '90s<sup id="cite_ref-planetworldcup.com_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-planetworldcup.com-1">[1]</a></sup> and the greatest Romanian footballer of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Galatasaray_S.K._(football)" title="Galatasaray S.K. (football)">Galatasaray</a> fans called him "<i>Comandante</i>" ("The Commander") and Romanians call him "<i>Regele</i>" ("The King").<sup id="cite_ref-Romania_and_Gala’s_commander_and_king_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Romania_and_Gala’s_commander_and_king-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>Nicknamed "The <a href="/wiki/Diego_Maradona" title="Diego Maradona">Maradona</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains" title="Carpathian Mountains">Carpathians</a>", Hagi is considered a hero in his homeland. He was named <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Footballer_of_the_Year" title="Romanian Footballer of the Year">Romanian Footballer of the Year</a> seven times, and is regarded as one of the best football players of his generation.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-soccer_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-soccer-5">[5]</a></sup> As a creative advanced <a href="/wiki/Playmaker" title="Playmaker">playmaker</a>, he was renowned for his dribbling, technique, vision, passing and finishing.<sup id="cite_ref-Romania_and_Gala’s_commander_and_king_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Romania_and_Gala’s_commander_and_king-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FIFA_Profile_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIFA_Profile-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hagi played for the <a href="/wiki/Romania_national_football_team" title="Romania national football team">Romania national team</a> in three <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cups</a>, in <a href="/wiki/1990_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1990 FIFA World Cup">1990</a>, <a href="/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1994 FIFA World Cup">1994</a> (where he was named in the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_awards#All-Star_Team" title="FIFA World Cup awards">World Cup All-Star Team</a>) and <a href="/wiki/1998_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1998 FIFA World Cup">1998</a>; as well as in three <a href="/wiki/UEFA_European_Championship" title="UEFA European Championship">UEFA European Championships</a>, in <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1984" title="UEFA Euro 1984">1984</a>, <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1996" title="UEFA Euro 1996">1996</a> and <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2000" title="UEFA Euro 2000">2000</a>. He won a total of 125 caps for Romania, ranked second after <a href="/wiki/Dorinel_Munteanu" title="Dorinel Munteanu">Dorinel Munteanu</a>, and is the joint leading goalscorer (alongside <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Mutu" title="Adrian Mutu">Adrian Mutu</a>) with 35 goals.</p>
<p>In November 2003, to celebrate <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a>'s Jubilee, Hagi was selected as the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Jubilee_Awards" title="UEFA Jubilee Awards">Golden Player</a> of Romania by the <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Football_Federation" title="Romanian Football Federation">Romanian Football Federation</a> as their most outstanding player of the past 50 years.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> In 2004, he was named by <a href="/wiki/Pel%C3%A9" title="Pelé">Pelé</a> as one of the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_100" title="FIFA 100">125 Greatest Living Footballers</a> at a <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> Awards Ceremony.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> He was listed at number 25 in <i><a href="/wiki/World_Soccer_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="World Soccer Magazine">World Soccer Magazine</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s list of the 100 greatest players of the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-soccer_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-soccer-5">[5]</a></sup> Hagi is one of the few footballers to have played for both Spanish rival clubs Real Madrid and Barcelona.</p>
<p>In 2009, Hagi founded Romanian club <a href="/wiki/FC_Viitorul_Constan%C8%9Ba" title="FC Viitorul Constanța">Viitorul Constanța</a>. He is currently both owner and chairman of the club. Hagi also established the <a href="/wiki/Gheorghe_Hagi_football_academy" class="mw-redirect" title="Gheorghe Hagi football academy">Gheorghe Hagi football academy</a>, one of the biggest football academies in <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Southeastern Europe">Southeastern Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gheorghe_Hagi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Club career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Born in <a href="/wiki/S%C4%83cele,_Constan%C8%9Ba" title="Săcele, Constanța">Săcele</a>, Hagi started his career playing for the youth teams of <a href="/wiki/SSC_Farul_Constan%C8%9Ba" title="SSC Farul Constanța">Farul Constanța</a> in the 1970s, before being selected by the <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Football_Federation" title="Romanian Football Federation">Romanian Football Federation</a> to join the squad of Luceafărul București in 1980 for two years. In 1982, he returned to <a href="/wiki/Constan%C8%9Ba" title="Constanța">Constanța</a>, but one year later, aged 18, he was prepared to make the step to a top team. He was originally directed to <a href="/wiki/FC_Universitatea_Craiova" class="mw-redirect" title="FC Universitatea Craiova">Universitatea Craiova</a>, but chose <a href="/wiki/FC_Sportul_Studen%C8%9Besc_Bucure%C8%99ti" title="FC Sportul Studențesc București">Sportul Studențesc</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">Bucharest</a> instead.</p>
<p>In late 1987, Hagi transferred to <a href="/wiki/FC_Steaua_Bucure%C8%99ti" title="FC Steaua București">Steaua București</a> as the team prepared for their <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Super_Cup" title="UEFA Super Cup">European Super Cup</a> final against <a href="/wiki/FC_Dynamo_Kyiv" title="FC Dynamo Kyiv">Dynamo Kyiv</a>. The original contract was for one game only, the final. However, after winning the trophy, where Hagi scored the only goal of the match, Steaua did not want to release him back to Sportul Studențesc and retained him. During his Steaua years (1987–1990), Hagi played 97 <a href="/wiki/Liga_I" title="Liga I">Liga I</a> games, scoring 76 goals. He and the team reached the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">European Cup</a> semi-final in <a href="/wiki/1987%E2%80%9388_European_Cup" title="1987–88 European Cup">1988</a> and the <a href="/wiki/1989_European_Cup_Final" title="1989 European Cup Final">final</a> in the following year, while Hagi finished as one of the competition's top scorers in the former edition of the tournament. Hagi and Steaua were the champions of Romania in 1987, 1988 and 1989 and as well as winning the <a href="/wiki/Cupa_Rom%C3%A2niei" title="Cupa României">Cupa României</a> in 1987, 1988 and 1989. His strong performances had him linked with <a href="/wiki/Arrigo_Sacchi" title="Arrigo Sacchi">Arrigo Sacchi</a>'s <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">Milan</a> and <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a>, but <a href="/wiki/Nicolae_Ceau%C8%99escu" title="Nicolae Ceaușescu">Nicolae Ceaușescu</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Romania" title="Socialist Republic of Romania">communist government</a> rejected any offer.</p>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/1990_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1990 FIFA World Cup">1990 FIFA World Cup</a>, Hagi was signed by <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a>. The <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">La Liga</a> side paid $4.3&#160;million to Steaua București for him. Hagi played two seasons with Madrid, then was sold to <a href="/wiki/Brescia_Calcio" title="Brescia Calcio">Brescia</a>.</p>
<p>Hagi began the <a href="/wiki/1992%E2%80%9393_Serie_A" title="1992–93 Serie A">1992–93 season</a> with Brescia, but after his first season, the club was relegated to <a href="/wiki/Serie_B" title="Serie B">Serie B</a>. The next season, Hagi helped the club win <a href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_Serie_B" title="1993–94 Serie B">Serie B</a> and earn promotion back to <a href="/wiki/Serie_A" title="Serie A">Serie A</a>. After performing memorably during the <a href="/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1994 FIFA World Cup">1994 World Cup</a>, Hagi was signed by <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a>.</p>
<p>After two years at <i>Barça</i>, Hagi signed for Turkish club <a href="/wiki/Galatasaray_S.K._(football)" title="Galatasaray S.K. (football)">Galatasaray</a>. At Galatasaray, he was both successful and highly popular among the Turkish supporters. Hagi was an important member of a team that would win four consecutive league titles. In 2000, at age 35, Hagi had the best days of his career winning every possible trophy with Galatasaray. Gala won the <a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_UEFA_Cup" title="1999–2000 UEFA Cup">1999–2000 UEFA Cup</a> after defeating <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2000_UEFA_Cup_Final" title="2000 UEFA Cup Final">final</a>, a match in which Hagi was sent off for punching Arsenal captain <a href="/wiki/Tony_Adams" title="Tony Adams">Tony Adams</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> This was followed by the capture of the <a href="/wiki/2000_UEFA_Super_Cup" title="2000 UEFA Super Cup">UEFA Super Cup</a> with a historic win against Hagi's former club Real Madrid. Both feats were firsts, and remain unmatched in Turkish football history. The mass hysteria caused by these wins in <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a> raised Hagi's popularity even further with the fans and prompted <a href="/wiki/France_national_football_team" title="France national football team">French ex-international</a> <a href="/wiki/Luis_Fern%C3%A1ndez" title="Luis Fernández">Luis Fernández</a> to say, "Hagi is like wine, the older it gets, the better he is."</p>
<p>When he retired in 2001, Hagi remained one of the most beloved players in the Turkish and Romanian championships. Hagi is highly praised by the Galatasaray supporters. The classic chant "I Love You Hagi" was adopted by Gala fans since his arrival at Galatasaray.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gheorghe_Hagi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: International career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Hagi made his debut for the <a href="/wiki/Romania_national_football_team" title="Romania national football team">Romania national team</a> at age 18 in 1983 against <a href="/wiki/Norway_national_football_team" title="Norway national football team">Norway</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Oslo" title="Oslo">Oslo</a>. He was part of the Romanian team until 2000.</p>
<p>Hagi took part at the 1990 World Cup and later led the Romanian team to its best ever international performance at the 1994 World Cup, where the team reached the quarterfinals before <a href="/wiki/Sweden_national_football_team" title="Sweden national football team">Sweden</a> ended their run after winning the penalty shoot-out. Hagi scored three times in the tournament, including a memorable goal in their 3–2 surprise defeat of South American powerhouse and previous runners-up <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_football_team" title="Argentina national football team">Argentina</a>. In the first of Romania's group stage matches, against <a href="/wiki/Colombia_national_football_team" title="Colombia national football team">Colombia</a>, Hagi scored one of the most memorable goals of that tournament, curling in a 40-yard lob over Colombian goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/%C3%93scar_C%C3%B3rdoba" title="Óscar Córdoba">Óscar Córdoba</a> who was caught out of position. He was named in the Team of the Tournament.</p>
<p>Four years later, after the <a href="/wiki/1998_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1998 FIFA World Cup">1998 World Cup</a>, Hagi decided to retire from the national team, only to change his mind after a few months and participate in <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2000" title="UEFA Euro 2000">UEFA Euro 2000</a>, during which he was <a href="/wiki/Sent_off" class="mw-redirect" title="Sent off">sent off</a> in the quarter-final loss against <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2000_Final" title="UEFA Euro 2000 Final">eventual runners-up</a> <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hagi retired from professional football in 2001, age 36, in a game called "Gala Hagi" on 24 April. He still holds the record as Romanian national team top scorer.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_as_coach">Career as coach</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gheorghe_Hagi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Career as coach">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Romania_national_team">Romania national team</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gheorghe_Hagi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Romania national team">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2001, Hagi was named the manager of the Romania national team, replacing <a href="/wiki/Ladislau_B%C3%B6l%C3%B6ni" class="mw-redirect" title="Ladislau Bölöni">Ladislau Bölöni</a>, who left the squad to coach <a href="/wiki/Sporting_Clube_de_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Sporting Clube de Portugal">Sporting Clube de Portugal</a>. After failing to qualify the team for the <a href="/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2002 FIFA World Cup">World Cup</a>, however, Hagi was sacked. His only notable achievement during the six months as Romania's manager was the win in <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a> against <a href="/wiki/Hungary_national_football_team" title="Hungary national football team">Hungary</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bursaspor">Bursaspor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gheorghe_Hagi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Bursaspor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2003, Hagi took over as coach of Turkish <a href="/wiki/S%C3%BCper_Lig" title="Süper Lig">Süper Lig</a> side <a href="/wiki/Bursaspor" title="Bursaspor">Bursaspor</a>, but left the club after a disappointing start to the season.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Galatasaray">Galatasaray</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gheorghe_Hagi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Galatasaray">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Hagi then became manager of Galatasaray in 2004, leading the team to the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Cup" title="Turkish Cup">Turkish Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/2005_Turkish_Cup_Final" title="2005 Turkish Cup Final">2005 final</a> with 5–1 as a score against <a href="/wiki/Fenerbah%C3%A7e%E2%80%93Galatasaray_rivalry" class="mw-redirect" title="Fenerbahçe–Galatasaray rivalry">fierce rivals</a> <a href="/wiki/Fenerbah%C3%A7e_S.K._(football)" title="Fenerbahçe S.K. (football)">Fenerbahçe</a>. His contract, however, was not renewed since his team was not able to win <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_S%C3%BCper_Lig" title="2004–05 Süper Lig">2004–05 Süper Lig</a> title over Fenerbahçe during the <a href="/wiki/Centennial" title="Centennial">centennial</a> of the club.</p>
<h3><span id="Politehnica_Timi.C8.99oara"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Politehnica_Timișoara">Politehnica Timișoara</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gheorghe_Hagi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Politehnica Timișoara">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Steaua București sought to hire Hagi in the summer of 2005, but Hagi's requested wage could not be met by the Romanian champions, and he became manager of <a href="/wiki/FC_Politehnica_Timi%C8%99oara" title="FC Politehnica Timișoara">Politehnica Timișoara</a> instead. However, after a string of poor results and disagreements with management, he left the club after a few months. Constanța's <a href="/wiki/Stadionul_Farul" title="Stadionul Farul">main stadium</a> used to bear his name, but the name was changed after Hagi signed with Politehnica Timișoara.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Steaua_Bucure.C8.99ti"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Steaua_București">Steaua București</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gheorghe_Hagi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Steaua București">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From June to September 2007, Hagi coached Steaua București, had a mediocre start in the internal championship mainly due to the large number of unavailable injured players, and managed to qualify the team for the second time in line to the UEFA Champions League group stages, passing two qualifying rounds. He resigned due to a long series of conflicts with club owner <a href="/wiki/Gigi_Becali" title="Gigi Becali">Gigi Becali</a>, which also happens to be his godson. The main reason for resigning was the owner's policy of imposing players, making the team's strategy and threats. Hagi's resigned mere hours after Steaua's first Champions League match away against <a href="/wiki/SK_Slavia_Prague" title="SK Slavia Prague">Slavia Prague</a>, a 2–1 loss.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Galatasaray_return">Galatasaray return</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gheorghe_Hagi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Galatasaray return">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After <a href="/wiki/Frank_Rijkaard" title="Frank Rijkaard">Frank Rijkaard</a> was sacked as coach, Hagi signed a one and a half year contract with Galatasaray on 21 October 2010. His official presentation was held on 22 October.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> His former teammate from Galatasaray <a href="/wiki/Tugay_Kerimo%C4%9Flu" title="Tugay Kerimoğlu">Tugay Kerimoğlu</a> assisted him in <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>, but he was sacked on 22 March 2011 after a series of poor results in the Süper Lig.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_of_play">Style of play</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gheorghe_Hagi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Style of play">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>A talented left-footed <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Attacking_midfielder" title="Midfielder">attacking midfielder</a>, Hagi's playing style was frequently <a href="/wiki/New_Maradona" title="New Maradona">compared</a> with <a href="/wiki/Diego_Maradona" title="Diego Maradona">Diego Maradona</a>'s throughout his career, due to his technical ability as well as his temperamental character and leadership;<sup id="cite_ref-treccani_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-treccani-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gheorghe_Hagi:_The_Maradona_of_the_Carpathians_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gheorghe_Hagi:_The_Maradona_of_the_Carpathians-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-zonacesarini_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zonacesarini-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> as a youth, he was mainly inspired by compatriots <a href="/wiki/Anghel_Iord%C4%83nescu" title="Anghel Iordănescu">Anghel Iordănescu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ion_Dumitru" title="Ion Dumitru">Ion Dumitru</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Gheorghe_Hagi:_The_Maradona_of_the_Carpathians_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gheorghe_Hagi:_The_Maradona_of_the_Carpathians-15">[15]</a></sup> A quick, highly creative, and mobile advanced <a href="/wiki/Playmaker" title="Playmaker">playmaker</a>, Hagi was also tactically versatile, and capable of playing in several <a href="/wiki/Midfielder" title="Midfielder">midfield</a> and <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)" title="Forward (association football)">offensive</a> positions on either <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Winger" title="Midfielder">wing</a> or through the <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Central_midfielder" title="Midfielder">middle</a>, due to his ability with both feet, despite being naturally left-footed, although he had a preference for using his stronger foot; his preferred position was in a free role as a classic number 10, but he was also used as a <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)#Second_striker" title="Forward (association football)">second striker</a> on occasion.<sup id="cite_ref-planetworldcup.com_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-planetworldcup.com-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Romania_and_Gala’s_commander_and_king_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Romania_and_Gala’s_commander_and_king-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-zonacesarini_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zonacesarini-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-legacy_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-legacy-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rare_No._10_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rare_No._10-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Hagi was renowned in particular for his first touch and speed on the ball, as well as his timing, interpretation of space, bursts of acceleration, and <a href="/wiki/Dribbling#Association_football" title="Dribbling">dribbling</a> skills, which enabled him to get past defenders; he was also highly regarded for his vision and precise passing,<sup id="cite_ref-planetworldcup.com_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-planetworldcup.com-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Romania_and_Gala’s_commander_and_king_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Romania_and_Gala’s_commander_and_king-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-zonacesarini_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zonacesarini-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> although he was capable of both scoring and assisting goals, and was also an accurate finisher and <a href="/wiki/Direct_free_kick" title="Direct free kick">set-piece</a> taker, who had a penchant for scoring goals from powerful, <a href="/wiki/Curl_(football)" title="Curl (football)">bending</a> long range strikes.<sup id="cite_ref-planetworldcup.com_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-planetworldcup.com-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Romania_and_Gala’s_commander_and_king_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Romania_and_Gala’s_commander_and_king-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gheorghe_Hagi:_The_Maradona_of_the_Carpathians_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gheorghe_Hagi:_The_Maradona_of_the_Carpathians-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-zonacesarini_16-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zonacesarini-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-legacy_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-legacy-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-virtuoso_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-virtuoso-24">[24]</a></sup> In spite of his small stature, Hagi possessed significant upper body strength, which, along with his control, aided him in protecting the ball from opponents, and allowed him to create space for himself or his teammates.<sup id="cite_ref-Gheorghe_Hagi:_The_Maradona_of_the_Carpathians_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gheorghe_Hagi:_The_Maradona_of_the_Carpathians-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-legacy_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-legacy-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Despite his skill and his reputation as one of the greatest <a href="/wiki/Squad_number_(association_football)" title="Squad number (association football)">number 10s</a> of his generation, his career was marked by inconsistency at times, and he was also considered to be a controversial player, due to his rebellious and arrogant attitude, as well as his low work-rate and lack of discipline, which led him to have several disagreements with his managers, opponents, and officials.<sup id="cite_ref-Gheorghe_Hagi:_The_Maradona_of_the_Carpathians_15-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gheorghe_Hagi:_The_Maradona_of_the_Carpathians-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rare_No._10_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rare_No._10-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hagi's_step_too_far_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hagi's_step_too_far-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Perfect_10_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Perfect_10-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gheorghe_Hagi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>His son <a href="/wiki/Ianis_Hagi" title="Ianis Hagi">Ianis</a>, who is also a footballer was born in <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, when he was playing for <a href="/wiki/Galatasaray_S.K._(football)" title="Galatasaray S.K. (football)">Galatasaray SK</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_statistics">Career statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gheorghe_Hagi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Career statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Club">Club</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gheorghe_Hagi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Club">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Individual">Individual</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gheorghe_Hagi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Individual">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Liga_I" title="Liga I">Romanian League</a>: Top Scorer 1985, 1986<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup#All-star_team" title="1994 FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup All-Star Team</a>: 1994<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/World_Soccer_Magazine#The_Greatest_Players_of_the_20th_century" class="mw-redirect" title="World Soccer Magazine"><i>World Soccer Magazine</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s 100 Greatest Players of the 20th century</a>: 1999 (#25)<sup id="cite_ref-soccer_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-soccer-5">[5]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/UEFA_Jubilee_Awards" title="UEFA Jubilee Awards">UEFA Jubilee Awards</a> – <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Jubilee_Awards" title="UEFA Jubilee Awards">Greatest Romanian Footballer of the last 50 Years</a>: 2003<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/FIFA_100" title="FIFA 100">FIFA 100</a>: 2004<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Golden_Foot#Award_legends" title="Golden Foot">Golden Foot Legends Award</a>: 2015<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Romania_Coach_of_the_Year" title="Romania Coach of the Year">Romania Coach of the Year</a>: 2015, 2017<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup></li>

Retrieved <span class="nowrap">20 December</span> 2017</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Gazeta+Sporturilor&amp;rft.atitle=Hagi+e+antrenorul+anului+2017+%C3%AEn+ancheta+Gazetei%21+Pentru+c%C4%83+ne+%C3%AEnve%C8%9Bi+s%C4%83+nu+ced%C4%83m+%C3%AEn+meserie%2C+mul%C8%9Bumim%2C+Gic%C4%83%21+%C2%BB+Iat%C4%83+%C8%99i+ceilal%C8%9Bi+3+laurea%C8%9Bi&amp;rft.date=2017-12-20&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.gsp.ro%2Fgsp-special%2Fanchetele-gazetei%2Fhagi-e-antrenorul-anului-2017-in-ancheta-gazetei-pentru-ca-ne-inveti-sa-nu-cedam-in-meserie-multumim-gica-iata-si-ceilalti-3-laureati-528553.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGheorghe+Hagi" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>

<div id="European_Cup_and_UEFA_Champions_League_top_scorers" style="font-size:114%;margin:0 4em"><a href="/wiki/List_of_European_Cup_and_UEFA_Champions_League_top_scorers" title="List of European Cup and UEFA Champions League top scorers">European Cup and UEFA Champions League top scorers</a></div>

<tr>
<th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="background: gold;;width:1%">European Cup</th>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-odd hlist" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
<ul>
<li>1955–56: <a href="/wiki/Milo%C5%A1_Milutinovi%C4%87" title="Miloš Milutinović">Milutinović</a></li>
<li>1956–57: <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Viollet" title="Dennis Viollet">Viollet</a></li>
<li>1957–58: <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Di_St%C3%A9fano" title="Alfredo Di Stéfano">Di Stéfano</a></li>
<li>1958–59: <a href="/wiki/Just_Fontaine" title="Just Fontaine">Fontaine</a></li>
<li>1959–60: <a href="/wiki/Ferenc_Pusk%C3%A1s" title="Ferenc Puskás">Puskás</a></li>
<li>1960–61: <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_%C3%81guas" title="José Águas">J. Águas</a></li>
<li>1961–62: <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Di_St%C3%A9fano" title="Alfredo Di Stéfano">Di Stéfano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bent_L%C3%B8fqvist" title="Bent Løfqvist">Løfqvist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ferenc_Pusk%C3%A1s" title="Ferenc Puskás">Puskás</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heinz_Strehl" title="Heinz Strehl">Strehl</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Justo_Tejada" title="Justo Tejada">Tejada</a></li>
<li>1962–63: <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Altafini" title="José Altafini">Altafini</a></li>
<li>1963–64: <a href="/wiki/Vladica_Kova%C4%8Devi%C4%87" title="Vladica Kovačević">Kovačević</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sandro_Mazzola" title="Sandro Mazzola">Mazzola</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Ferenc_Pusk%C3%A1s" title="Ferenc Puskás">Puskás</a></li>
<li>1964–65: <a href="/wiki/Eus%C3%A9bio" title="Eusébio">Eusébio</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Augusto_Torres" title="José Augusto Torres">Torres</a></li>
<li>1965–66: <a href="/wiki/Fl%C3%B3ri%C3%A1n_Albert" title="Flórián Albert">Albert</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Eus%C3%A9bio" title="Eusébio">Eusébio</a></li>
<li>1966–67: <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Piepenburg" title="Jürgen Piepenburg">Piepenburg</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Paul_Van_Himst" title="Paul Van Himst">Van Himst</a></li>
<li>1967–68: <a href="/wiki/Eus%C3%A9bio" title="Eusébio">Eusébio</a></li>
<li>1968–69: <a href="/wiki/Denis_Law" title="Denis Law">Law</a></li>
<li>1969–70: <a href="/wiki/Mick_Jones_(footballer,_born_1945)" title="Mick Jones (footballer, born 1945)">Jones</a></li>
<li>1970–71: <a href="/wiki/Antonis_Antoniadis" title="Antonis Antoniadis">Antoniadis</a></li>
<li>1971–72: <a href="/wiki/Antal_Dunai" title="Antal Dunai">Dunai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lou_Macari" title="Lou Macari">Macari</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Silvester_Taka%C4%8D" title="Silvester Takač">Takač</a></li>
<li>1972–73: <a href="/wiki/Gerd_M%C3%BCller" title="Gerd Müller">Müller</a></li>
<li>1973–74: <a href="/wiki/Gerd_M%C3%BCller" title="Gerd Müller">Müller</a></li>
<li>1974–75: <a href="/wiki/Gerd_M%C3%BCller" title="Gerd Müller">Müller</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Eduard_Markarov" title="Eduard Markarov">Markarov</a></li>
<li>1975–76: <a href="/wiki/Jupp_Heynckes" title="Jupp Heynckes">Heynckes</a></li>
<li>1976–77: <a href="/wiki/Franco_Cucinotta" title="Franco Cucinotta">Cucinotta</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Gerd_M%C3%BCller" title="Gerd Müller">Müller</a></li>
<li>1977–78: <a href="/wiki/Allan_Simonsen" title="Allan Simonsen">Simonsen</a></li>
<li>1978–79: <a href="/wiki/Claudio_Sulser" title="Claudio Sulser">Sulser</a></li>
<li>1979–80: <a href="/wiki/S%C3%B8ren_Lerby" title="Søren Lerby">Lerby</a></li>
<li>1980–81: <a href="/wiki/Terry_McDermott" title="Terry McDermott">McDermott</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karl-Heinz_Rummenigge" title="Karl-Heinz Rummenigge">Rummenigge</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Graeme_Souness" title="Graeme Souness">Souness</a></li>
<li>1981–82: <a href="/wiki/Dieter_Hoene%C3%9F" title="Dieter Hoeneß">Hoeneß</a></li>
<li>1982–83: <a href="/wiki/Paolo_Rossi" title="Paolo Rossi">Rossi</a></li>
<li>1983–84: <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Sokol_(footballer,_born_1954)" title="Viktor Sokol (footballer, born 1954)">Sokol</a></li>
<li>1984–85: <a href="/wiki/Torbj%C3%B6rn_Nilsson" title="Torbjörn Nilsson">Nilsson</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Michel_Platini" title="Michel Platini">Platini</a></li>
<li>1985–86: <a href="/wiki/Torbj%C3%B6rn_Nilsson" title="Torbjörn Nilsson">Nilsson</a></li>
<li>1986–87: <a href="/wiki/Borislav_Cvetkovi%C4%87" title="Borislav Cvetković">Cvetković</a></li>
<li>1987–88: <a href="/wiki/Rui_%C3%81guas_(footballer)" title="Rui Águas (footballer)">R. Águas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jean-Marc_Ferreri" title="Jean-Marc Ferreri">Ferreri</a>, <a class="mw-selflink selflink">Hagi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rabah_Madjer" title="Rabah Madjer">Madjer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ally_McCoist" title="Ally McCoist">McCoist</a>, <a href="/wiki/M%C3%ADchel_(footballer)" title="Míchel (footballer)">Míchel</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Petar_Nov%C3%A1k" title="Petar Novák">Novák</a></li>
<li>1988–89: <a href="/wiki/Marco_van_Basten" title="Marco van Basten">Van Basten</a></li>
<li>1989–90: <a href="/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Papin" title="Jean-Pierre Papin">Papin</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Rom%C3%A1rio" title="Romário">Romário</a></li>
<li>1990–91: <a href="/wiki/Peter_Pacult" title="Peter Pacult">Pacult</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Papin" title="Jean-Pierre Papin">Papin</a></li>
<li>1991–92: <a href="/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Papin" title="Jean-Pierre Papin">Papin</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Yuran" title="Sergei Yuran">Yuran</a></li>

<li>1998–99: <a href="/wiki/Andriy_Shevchenko" title="Andriy Shevchenko">Shevchenko</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Dwight_Yorke" title="Dwight Yorke">Yorke</a></li>
<li>1999–2000: <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1rio_Jardel" title="Mário Jardel">Jardel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_(footballer)" title="Raúl (footballer)">Raúl</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Rivaldo" title="Rivaldo">Rivaldo</a></li>
<li>2000–01: <a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_(footballer)" title="Raúl (footballer)">Raúl</a></li>
<li>2001–02: <a href="/wiki/Ruud_van_Nistelrooy" title="Ruud van Nistelrooy">Van Nistelrooy</a></li>

<td colspan="2" class="navbox-list navbox-odd" style="width:100%;padding:0px;font-size:114%;">
